The Grain Market: Sunny Weather Causes the River Rice Market to Weaken 122

▲ Nantou: Yesterday, the supply of goods arriving via the Xiang Road continued, and the upward trend subsided slightly. Boat shipments opened at nearly 1,000 shi per boat. Various shops did not respond by adding more stock, and customers were also affected. Xixin (new west) and Sutong (Suzhou-Tongzhou) japonica rice each weakened by 2 jiǎo. The supply of Yaozhong (kiln-dried) Baige rice increased, but the local market had a poor appetite, and the market for Ningbo rice was also small, with prices good at nearly 1 jiǎo. Yang Duijian (foreign Dujiang) and Baipo (white broken) rice from rural villages had some sales, and the outlook was firm. Glutinous rice and white paddy rice sales were slow. The situation fluctuated.

▲ Xinzha: Yesterday, there were over 40 suppliers. The retail sales of Zhongguan (central customs) goods also showed no improvement, and shop owners felt increasingly stuck. The market appeared weak. Chonggu (Chongming-Guji) Qingjiao (green horn) and Fenglian (maple training) varieties were ignored, and prices were reduced by 1 or 2 jiǎo. The supply of Xixin (new west) japonica rice and Tingyin rice was not large, and sales were also slow, with prices reduced by another 2 jiǎo. The supply of Bujian (pier head) rice was not strong, and river merchants and factories had some inventory. Various firms slightly increased their spot sales of small Jiaomi (milled rice), but transactions were not smooth, and opening prices decreased.

The Forward Foreign Rice Market is Very Active 123

Yesterday's foreign rice market: Spot prices were mainly watched by locals due to the fall in the forward market, so the market only saw about 1,000 bags of small Jiaoxiao (milled rice) from Saigon being dealt with for local needs. Market prices were similar to the previous day. Forward trading remained active. In addition to local purchases, merchants from the Yangtze River region also inquired. Foreign firms were happy to attract business because the gold price had fallen back and transportation was cost-effective. The whole market saw Jinlong Foreign Firm selling 2,000 tons of April-May small Jiaoxiao and Tianxiang selling 1,500 tons, both at 5 taels and 1 qián. Tianxiang also sold 500 tons each of November-December Saigon No. 1 rice, and bought back several hundred tons of small Jiaoxiao for immediate loading and December delivery. Market prices were lower than the previous day, likely due to the influence of the gold market.

The Marked Powder Market is About to Collapse 124

Yesterday, after the opening of both the morning and afternoon powder markets, the market for various months suddenly showed signs of instability. Although the quotation for foreign wheat had rebounded by 3 or 4 jiǎo, the gold market had weakened, and the exchange rate was increasing. From this, it was speculated that the rise in foreign wheat prices would inevitably be hampered again. This situation of easy rise and fall was difficult to grasp for the time being. The situation abroad could not be predicted. Because of this situation, sentiment turned soft, and selling pressure gradually increased, falling by 2 or 3 fēn compared to the peak of the previous day. However, sentiment gradually stabilized at the close. As a result, this month's contract fell by 1.5 fēn compared to the previous day, December fell by 2 fēn, January fell by 1 fēn, February fell by 1 fēn and 2 lí and a half, March fell by 2 fēn, and April fell by 1 fēn.

Forward Wheat in a Declining Market 125

Yesterday, after the opening of both the morning and afternoon forward wheat markets, the market for various months showed signs of weakening. Although the price of foreign wheat had rebounded by 3 or 4 jiǎo, the gold price was falling, and the exchange rate was increasing, so there was hope for fixed securities in the future. Therefore, most people, learning from previous mistakes, inevitably became apprehensive. Although large sell-offs did not occur, sentiment softened. Observing future developments, if the gold market falls again, the market will still be weak and sluggish. As a result, this month's contract fell by 5 fēn compared to the previous day, December fell by 4 fēn, January fell by 4 fēn, February fell by 3 fēn, March fell by 5 fēn, and April fell by 3 fēn.

Local News

The Representatives of the Beijing-Guangdong Peace Conference Continued to Hold the Sixth Preparatory Meeting Yesterday 131

▲ Passed the National Fiscal Reorganization Committee Proposal

▲ The Fourth Plenary Session Has Been Discussed and a Solution Has Been Found

▲ The Seventh Preparatory Meeting Will Be Held This Morning

▲ The Petition Process of Representatives from Labor and Academic Circles

The Beijing and Guangdong representatives held a discussion meeting at 9:30 yesterday morning at the Wu residence. At 10:30, they received dozens of petitioning representatives from labor and academic circles. At 4:00 in the afternoon, they continued to hold the sixth preparatory meeting, passing the proposal to establish a National Fiscal Reorganization Committee. It was decided that the seventh preparatory meeting would be held at 9:00 this morning. At that time, the Beijing representative, Zhang Ji, will come to Shanghai from Beijing to attend, report on the issues of the Fourth Plenary Session, convey the intentions of the Beijing side, and discuss compromise solutions. The news obtained yesterday is summarized below:

Morning Discussion Meeting 132

The representatives arrived one after another at 9:20 in the morning. After a brief rest, they began the discussion meeting at 9:30. The Guangdong representatives, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, Wu Chaoshu, Chen Youren, and Zou Lu, all attended. From the Nanjing side, except for Zhang Ji, who remained in Beijing to negotiate, and Li Shizeng, who was absent due to illness, the remaining four representatives, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Jingjiang, and Chen Mingshu, all attended. Both sides continued to discuss the issue of convening the Fourth National Congress, and the discussion was mostly completed by 10:30. Because representatives from labor and academic circles had come to petition and needed to present their petitions in person, Wang Jingwei and Cai Yuanpei were publicly selected to represent both the Beijing and Guangdong sides and receive representatives from various schools, labor unions, and university professors, until noon. The Beijing and Guangdong representatives then continued their discussions, which concluded at 1:00, and it was decided to formally resume the sixth preparatory meeting at 4:00 in the afternoon.

Afternoon Sixth Meeting 133

At around 5:00 yesterday afternoon, the Beijing and Guangdong representatives gathered at the Wu residence and began the sixth preparatory meeting, which ended at 6:30. Yesterday, the interim chairman of the meeting, Wang Jingwei, issued a written summary of the sixth meeting, stating that on November 6, at 5:00 PM, the meeting continued at the Wu residence at No. 29 Gordon Road. The attending representatives were Wang Jingwei, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Jingjiang, Wu Chaoshu, Li Wenfan, Sun Ke, Zou Lu, Wu Tiecheng, Chen Mingshu, and Chen Youren. The chairman was Wang Zhaoming, and the recorders were Zhong Tianxin, Qiu Jinxian, and Yang Zongjiong. The resolutions were: (1) Regarding the establishment of a Fiscal Committee, the following items were passed: (A) A National Fiscal Committee will be established, and the government will grant it the following powers: (1) Reorganizing finance; (2) Reviewing budgets; (3) Reviewing the issuance of public bonds; (4) Auditing and verifying accounts; (5) Publishing income and expenditure accounts. (B) The Fiscal Committee will be organized by the following personnel: (1) Several government officials; (2) Several people from the banking industry; (3) Several people from industry and commerce; (4) Several economic scholars; (5) Several experienced experts. The number of people in each of the above categories must be equal. (2) The chairman of the Fiscal Committee will be concurrently held by the president of the Executive Yuan. (2) In order to prevent civil war, the central and local financial revenues, such as providing military expenditures, should be limited to national defense and bandit suppression. The Fiscal Committee may refuse to bear all burdens related to civil war. "Wang Zhaoming, 11.6."

Discussions on the Fourth Plenary Session Postponed 134

The issue of convening the Fourth Plenary Session was the focus of contention between the two sides. During the discussion meeting yesterday morning, the representatives repeatedly discussed it in order to find a compromise solution that would satisfy both governments. At the formal meeting in the afternoon, the Beijing representative, Zhang Ji, called from Beijing, stating that the Beijing side had discussed and found a proper solution to the issue of the Fourth Plenary Session. He requested that the issue not be resolved at today's meeting, and that he would return to Shanghai tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning) to attend the meeting, report in detail, and then proceed with a public vote. Therefore, the issue was not formally discussed at yesterday's meeting. It is expected that a considerable conclusion will be reached on this issue at the seventh preparatory meeting today.

List of Petitioning Representatives 135

At 10:30 yesterday morning, the representatives who went to the Wu residence to petition included the presidents and faculty members of nine universities: Sheng Zhenwei of Soochow University, Ou Yuanhuai of Great China University, Fu Shishuo and Wang Yuxiang of Shanghai University, Liu Zhanen and Zhang Chunjiang of Shanghai Baptist College, Chen Mengyu, Lu Fushan, and Gong Muyu of East Asia University, Shen Junru of Shanghai Law College, Quan Tongyin, Lin Jiyong, and Zhang Yi of Fudan University, Cao Liangxia and Zhao Enlang of Datong University, Li Zuohui and Liu Shijie of Jiangnan University, Hu Qibing and Rong Qizhao of Kwang Hua University. Representatives of the National Students Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation petitioning delegation included Chen Yaosheng from Zhejiang, Cao Zongzhi from Hunan, Han Jixian from Shanghai, Yang Yongyi from Shanxi, Zhu Songxi from Jiangsu, Yuan Jinzhang from Ningxia, Song Sixiang from Anhui, Yuan Qijiong from Nanjing, Li Yunqing from Shaanxi, Tang Guanglie from Hubei, Du Bingkang from Fujian, Zhang Chengxian from Henan, Shi Tonggang from the Association of Students Studying in Japan, and Yan Qingping from Tianjin. On the labor union side, the representatives who attended included the sign industry union, the inn and Beiyang reception union, the silk spitting union, the straw hat industry union, the leg industry union, the new clothing worker's union, the inn and Yangtze reception union, the Nanyang sock factory union, the Huiguan (Anhui guildhall) worker's union, the Nanhua (southern goods) worker's union, the Huafa (French-Chinese) cleaning union, the Taikang Food Company union, the Hongbai (red and white) timber industry union, the manufacturing peasant union, the scale industry union, the tea worker's union, the French business hydro-electric union, the Shengde manufacturing factory union, and the Shanghai Jeyin Newspaper Delivery union, and over one hundred other groups.

Situation of Receiving Representatives 136

When Mr. Wang and Mr. Cai received the representatives, the National Student Union first put forward five points: (1) Please report the past situation of the Peace Conference; (2) Please report the specific proposals for this conference; (3) State the resolutions of this conference: (A) If peace breaks down, a telegram will be sent to all schools across the country to strike; (B) This union believes that those who undermine peaceful unification are public enemies of the nation; (C) The Peace Conference should be open to the public; (4) Please limit the achievement of peaceful unification to before December 12th; (5) Before peaceful unification is achieved, please postpone the convening of the Fourth Plenary Session of the KMT between the Beijing and Guangdong sides.

Following this, the labor representatives stated their opinions, requesting the representatives of the Nanjing and Guangdong sides to continue discussing peaceful solutions in Shanghai. Before a solution is reached, the representatives should not go to Beijing for the time being, and two petitions were presented in person.

Then, representatives from various universities expressed their views. Initially, Cao Liangxia from Datong University stated the points of this petition, earnestly requesting the representatives of Nanjing and Guangdong to discard their differences and adopt the three points previously submitted by the union in writing. At this point, Liu Zhanen from Shanghai University also stated that since the incident in the East Province (Manchuria), the youth students in Shanghai have been extremely indignant. The Peace Conference has not yet reached a solution today, and the youth students all want to cry without a place to do so. He and others also hold positions as teachers and, seeing this situation, they really cannot lead the youth. Speaking to this point, Mr. Liu was choked with emotion and could not continue. After a long pause, he continued, "When the Pacific International Academic Conference was held in Shanghai previously, I was also one of the Chinese representatives. During the discussions, we also discussed the Japanese atrocities. I deeply feel that domestic peace and unity are so difficult to achieve. How can we seek external assistance? Therefore, I sincerely hope that the representatives of Nanjing and Guangdong will immediately discard their prejudices and work together to overcome the national crisis."

Next, Shen Junru from the Law School also expressed his views, deeply concerned that the peaceful unity of Nanjing and Guangdong cannot be achieved immediately. He also said that holding the Peace Conference in the concession, if it ends in failure, will surely be ridiculed by all nations. In the past, the Northern warlord Wu Peifu was scorned for seeking refuge in the concession after his defeat. You are all advanced members of the party and the country. This Peace Conference will surely be successful and seek a unified approach to foreign affairs.

When Mr. Shen spoke to this point, Zhang Yi from Fudan University was about to continue speaking when Mr. Wang Jingwei, the representative of Guangdong, suddenly became angry and said, "Please allow me to answer your questions first. If I cannot, I will withdraw from the meeting." Zhang then hesitated and stopped speaking. Then, Wang gave a detailed reply (record omitted). After Mr. Wang finished speaking, he continued to ask the representatives to express their opinions. Zhang Yi, the representative of Fudan University, spoke, requesting that the representatives achieve a peaceful solution within three days at the latest. If either the Nanjing or Guangdong sides intentionally obstruct it, the peaceful representatives of both sides should strive with their lives. This is the time for party members to sacrifice themselves for the country. Future generations will have their own judgment. Wang and others listened and applauded greatly, and expressed their complete acceptance. Then, Cai Yuanpei replied, roughly saying that based on the current trend, the Fourth Plenary Session should be held first, and then the government should be reorganized.

▲Two Petitions from Various Trade Unions (Petition One) 137

To the Esteemed Representatives of the Nanjing-Guangdong Peace Conference:

Unfortunately, our country has been weak for many years and has been frequently invaded by foreign powers. After the revolution, human affairs were still not stable. The traitor Yuan Shikai claimed himself emperor before, and Zhang Xun restored the monarchy after. Descending to Cao Kun and Wu Peifu, they exhausted their troops and engaged in constant warfare, with corpses lying everywhere. The country's vitality has been damaged and the nation's life almost extinguished. Fortunately, our party launched an expedition to the south, comforting the people and punishing the guilty. With the comrades advancing and falling one after another, and the compatriots working together with one heart, we were able to create a unified situation in the seventeenth year of the Republic. We hoped to stabilize society from then on, begin construction, secure the country like a lush mulberry tree, and place the people on comfortable mats. However, looking back at the past, things did not go as we wished. The warlords Cao Kun and Wu Peifu were overthrown by the armed forces of the entire nation, but those who followed Cao Kun and Wu Peifu are alive and well. As a result, the flames of war have repeatedly flared up. Recently, Japan has invaded, and Liaoning and Jilin have been occupied. The danger to the nation's lifeline is indeed unprecedented. At this time, the representatives of Guangdong were able to come without blaming the past, and the representatives of Nanjing were also able to be open and honest, and gathered in Shanghai for discussions. This is truly the great fortune of the country. Unexpectedly, after only a few days of discussion, the future is again presenting a pessimistic outlook. At this time when the nation's lifeline is hanging by a thread, our unions are deeply worried and cannot help but make some statements to the representatives:

(1) Regarding the important nature of the Peace Conference. Internally, the communists are rampant, and disaster victims are everywhere. Externally, powerful neighbors are invading and occupying our territory. This conference is the key to resisting foreign aggression and pacifying the country. If the conference unfortunately breaks down, the nation will be in increasing danger. Therefore, the representatives of Nanjing and Guangdong should proceed as quickly as possible to achieve unification, and should not affect the Peace Conference due to the issue of preserving the position of any individual, and plant disaster for the nation.

(2) Regarding the scope of discussion of the Peace Conference. The internal disintegration is the result of various bad causes, and these bad causes are the unsuitable fundamental system. Therefore, the scope of discussion of the Peace Conference should focus on the reform of the fundamental system. Regarding the reform of the fundamental system, the principle of separation of military and political affairs has already been decided at the previous conference, which is exactly what the people of the whole country support. Unexpectedly, a certain member of the Central Committee in Nanjing said that this fundamental system (text is suspected to be missing). It should be known that if this conference does not discuss the reform of the fundamental system, how can future disputes be eliminated? Currently, the fundamental reforms of the military and political systems have been decided, and the only item that has not been decided is party affairs. And the important matters of party affairs that must be decided in this conference are the same as the fundamental systems of military and political affairs that must be decided in the Peace Conference.

(3) Regarding the location of the conference. The location of the conference is closely related to the outcome of the Peace Conference. If it is bound by the military force of one side, and free will cannot be expressed, now it is heard that the Nanjing side is urging the representatives to go to Beijing for the meeting. Our unions believe that the location of the meeting can follow the example of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Second National Congress and be held in Shanghai, so that the representatives of both sides can have complete and full freedom of speech.

(4) Regarding diplomatic issues. Regarding diplomatic issues, it was previously heard that a consistent plan has been decided by both sides. What the plan is has not been disclosed in detail. However, our unions hope to recover the lost territories in the shortest possible time and protect our sovereignty. We must not repeat the mistakes of the past, allowing the Japanese army to trample on us and boast of non-resistance, allowing the territory to be lost and pretend to be calm. Now, based on the principle that everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the nation, we humbly offer our views for your consideration. If you are willing to accept what we have said, and achieve a permanent and genuine peace and unification, pacify the country and resist foreign aggression, we will rely on this one action, and we will be eagerly awaiting your orders.

Prepared by: Steering Committee of the Seamen's Union, Railway Engine Union, Silk Reeling Industry Union, Unions of Five Factories including Shenxin, Steering Committee of Dockworkers, First Cotton Mill Union of Tongxing, Railway Catering Union, Dongjiadu Ferry Workers Union, Anti-Japanese Association of Workers of Japanese Cotton Mills, Yufeng Cotton Mill Union, Xinyihe Textile Union, Hengfeng Cotton Mill Union, First Factory Union of Gongda, Donghua Cotton Mill Union of Japanese Merchants, First Cotton Mill Union of Japanese Merchants in Shanghai, First Cotton Mill Union of Internal and External Cotton, Fourth Cotton Mill Union of Shanghai, Journalists' Union, Yangjinggang Rowing Workers Union, Second Factory Union of Internal and External Cotton of Japanese Merchants, Fifth Cotton Mill Union of Shanghai, First Toyoda Cotton Mill Union, Tianzhang Paper Mill Union, Ninth Cotton Mill Union of Internal and External Cotton, Second and Third Cotton Mill Unions of Shanghai, Customs Huachang United Association, East Asia Jute Mill Union of Japanese Merchants, Steamboat Wood Industry Union, British American Tobacco Factory Union, Rowing Workers Union, Pudong Water and Wood Industry Union, First Xihe Cotton Mill Union, First Cotton Mill Union of Tongxing.

(Petition Two) Regarding the request to continue holding the Peace Conference in Shanghai in order to meet the people's expectations.

Since the opening of the Peace Conference, it has been almost ten days. The trade unions and others are eager for peace to be achieved as soon as possible in order to achieve a consistent effect of banning insults. However, peace is not achieved in the end, and resisting insults is really out of the question. You, gentlemen, have either traveled across oceans and mediated everywhere, or have come to Shanghai from thousands of miles away, originally wanting to seek the early realization of peace. How could it be known that your hard work for peaceful unification and national salvation would not be understood by others, but instead would be taken advantage of, and every effort would be made to entice you to go to Nanjing? You, gentlemen, should know that coming to Shanghai to seek peace was already a misstep. Planning for almost ten days has only gained the air of peace. If you go to Nanjing again, even the air of peace will disappear. The trade unions and others look to the future with unspeakable worries. We earnestly request you, gentlemen, to continue holding the meeting in Shanghai in order to complete the entire work of the Peace Conference and achieve the real effect of unification and resisting insults. The trade unions and others are overwhelmed with urgency and await your orders.

Respectfully presented to all the representatives of the Nanjing Peace and Unification Conference.

Temporary Executive Committee of the Shanghai General Labor Union, Shanghai Jieyin Newspaper Delivery Union, Shanghai Shengde Weaving Factory Union, Shanghai French Concession Water and Electricity Union, Shanghai Tea Industry Union, Shanghai Weighing Industry Union, Ink Making Union, Shanghai Taikang Food, Shanghai Nanyang Socks Factory Workers Union, Shanghai French Concession Cleaning Union, Shanghai Huiguan Staff Union, Shanghai Traveler's Changjiang Reception Union, Shanghai Leg Industry Union, Shanghai New Clothing Industry Union, Shanghai Straw Hat Industry Union, Shanghai Traveler's Nanhua Reception Union, Shanghai Traveler's Beiyang Reception Union, Shanghai Card Industry Union, Shanghai Silk Spit Union, Shanghai Customs Declaration Union, and more than seventy other trade unions.

▲Cai's Response to Student Representatives: Cai Yuanpei 138

Gave a reply, saying roughly: "Now China is united externally, and it can be said that it has achieved peaceful unification. What we are discussing is how to seek peace permanently in the future, but this is not a simple matter. Many past disputes and mistakes were not a matter of people, but partly a matter of the system. Changing the system should be decided by the Fourth National Congress of the Kuomintang, so Nanjing advocates holding the Fourth Plenary Session first. As for student strikes, this is what I am most opposed to. Today's students are the future leaders of China. For the sake of saving the country, they should pay attention to cultivating their own abilities and not take a dead end. Many patriotic people throw themselves into the sea and starve themselves because of the urgency of the national crisis. These are not solutions. In areas invaded by foreign enemies, it is impossible to study. Everyone sacrifices to save the country is out of necessity. Therefore, I advise students everywhere to concentrate on their studies and not use strikes as a slogan."

▲Wang's Talk to Labor and Student Representatives: Just Now 139

I heard what the labor and student representatives said, and I want to say something. I am representing the opinions of the comrades in Guangdong and giving a simple reply. Regarding the content of this Peace Conference, nothing is not public. All the proposals, except for a few, are published in the newspapers every day. The few that are not published are not intentionally kept secret. Moreover, there are three or two points that have not been published regarding diplomatic issues. This is certainly not because we are unwilling to make them public to our compatriots, but because diplomatic issues are not convenient for foreign countries to know. This is the reason why a very small number have not been published. I hope that all compatriots will forgive this point. Speaking of the progress of the Peace Conference, the first two days were about diplomatic issues. This is certainly for the sake of the national crisis, and of course, it must be dealt with urgently. Speaking of diplomatic issues, the Nanjing government has already obtained international recognition, so the negotiations should of course be done by the Nanjing government. However, the diplomatic guidelines and principles will be decided at this conference and handed over to the Nanjing government for implementation. Mr. Cai just said that the diplomatic situation is already unified, which is true. However, the so-called diplomatic unity of origin should be limited. For example, we certainly do not agree with the invasion of foreign troops without resistance or the loss of territory without anyone being responsible. This is not within the scope of diplomatic unity. In the following two days, this conference began to discuss the "Central Political System Reform Plan." Everyone should have seen these in the newspapers. The original intention of the Guangdong representatives in this trip was to first seek diplomatic unity externally, and then to have both sides organize a unified conference internally, and the unified conference would produce a unified government. After the new government is established, Mr. Jiang in Nanjing will resign immediately, and the Guangdong National Government will be abolished. Before this fact is implemented, both parties should make a statement to the people of their willingness to abolish them. That is to say, each party will issue a telegram. This was the original intention of Mr. Cai, Zhang, and Chen's consultations with us, and it is also the firm position of the Guangdong side. This is also the original intention of our coming to Shanghai for discussions. There is no need to hide this intention from everyone at all, because we feel that a country must have a government with unified power before it can show its strength externally, and only then can it seek the establishment of a foundation for democratic politics internally. We should not talk about the rights and wrongs of the past, but hurry up and start over to deal with this urgent situation. This is also the issue that the comrades of both sides in the Nanjing-Guangdong conference are humbly trying to solve. Mr. Cai just said that the Nanjing side's opinion later was that the Central Political System Reform Plan cannot be decided in this way and should be resolved in the Fourth Plenary Session. The original intention of Guangdong was to reorganize the government first, and then go to Nanjing to hold the Fourth Plenary Session. Nanjing thought that the reform of the central political system must be resolved in the Fourth Plenary Session, so they advocated holding the Fourth Plenary Session first. They also believed that the Japanese had already limited the withdrawal of troops to the 16th, so we should hold the Fourth Plenary Session in Nanjing before the 16th and before the 12th to show the unity of China. Therefore, the opinions of the two sides are different, and what is considered difficult now is this point. Some people asked me, "Why don't the Guangdong representatives go to Nanjing for the meeting?" This is because the Nanjing government has not been reorganized, so we should not go to Nanjing. There are many examples of holding meetings in Shanghai in the past. Wasn't there one held in Shanghai in December of the 16th year of the Republic? But perhaps it will be said that it is too unreasonable for you to hold meetings in Shanghai. Doesn't it show the cracks of division? I believe that the fact is still the fact. The fact that the Kuomintang is separated should be acknowledged. The student representatives just said that it is the responsibility of the party, which is correct. This responsibility should be borne by the Kuomintang. Today, Kuomintang members oppose the Kuomintang government. Don't think that the government of the Northern warlords and the government of Yuan Shikai are not party governments, so we should oppose them. The Nanjing government is a government created by the Kuomintang, so we are unwilling to oppose it. This is an unreasonable reason. We only ask whether this government is good or not, and do not ask whether it is a government created by the party or not. The worse the government created by the party, the more we party members should oppose it. Today's division is a fact. If we want to put on a show, hurry up and hold the Fourth Plenary Session on the 12th. Not to mention that the four hundred representatives from Guangdong cannot come to Nanjing, even six representatives will not easily enter. It is necessary to reorganize the government first and organize a government that everyone believes in and that the people support. Then we can enter Nanjing. Therefore, the different opinions of the two sides in the past few days are like this. All twelve of us representatives are working hard to find a good way, a way that both governments agree on. We are discussing this matter every day, and there is nothing that cannot be told to the public. I believe that in the future, in order to resolve China's disputes, there is no good way other than using political methods. Politics cannot be resolved by military means. Military resolution of political disputes will only mean that a military force will always exist, and China will never be good. Since the news of the Japanese soldiers' atrocities in the three northeastern provinces, neither side can use troops anymore, and war will certainly not be able to be reborn. Please rest assured, all representatives. However, in order to achieve the goal of resolving disputes and achieving lasting peace, we must have good methods and use political methods to organize a unified government. The principle of organizing a unified government should be democratization, so that it is in line with the principle of democracy. According to the program of the period of political tutelage in the Outline of National Construction, we must do it step by step. This statement means that during the period of political tutelage, in terms of time, civil rights are expanding day by day; in terms of space, civil rights are increasing day by day, from one county to one province, and to the whole country. Today's responsibility lies in being able to work together with one heart and one mind to transform the government successfully. This is not only the hope of every party member, but also the hope of the entire nation. But if it is said that the reorganization of the government must be resolved in the Fourth Plenary Session, then it is difficult. I remember that the National Government that was talked about was also reorganized by the Standing Committee after the closing of the Third Plenary Session in the 17th year of the Republic. The Standing Committee decided on the candidates for chairman and the candidates for the heads of the five branches of government. How can it be necessary to resolve it in the Fourth Plenary Session this time? Now is the time when the national crisis is at its height, and it is necessary to seek unity urgently. The opinions requested by the representatives are like this, and our stay here and our efforts to compromise are also like this. Fortunately, the representatives of both sides can discuss sincerely in order to achieve the goal of peaceful unification. Therefore, the future of peace is not without hope.

Wang's Response to University Representatives 140

You are all gentlemen of the intellectual world, and I am very willing to ask for advice. Since the 18th year of the Republic, I have been a person who has always opposed the Nanjing government. The Nanjing government is a party government. The meaning of my opposition is because all the political manifestations of the Nanjing government are military politics, not democratic politics. If it is thought that the party government is not good, and we cannot oppose it because of the face of the party, then this is not good for the party and not good for the principles. I am a member of the party and a member of the nation. What is not good about the party government? Not only party members should rise up to oppose it, but also the people should rise up to oppose it. Since the 18th year of the Republic, there has been fighting in the country every day. Is this government good or not? I hope you will make a judgment. If you think the government is not good, you should rise up to oppose the government. If you think we are not good, then please knock us down. If you think both of us are not good, then please knock both of us down. We must first recognize the rights and wrongs, and then the disputes of the party and the country can be resolved. Who does not want peace? But peace is not just a matter of words. There must be a way, and at the same time, we must look at all kinds of situations and the current situation. I just heard Mr. Shen say that in the midst of internal troubles and foreign enemies, our meeting in Shanghai and not entering Nanjing, and meeting in the concession, is not a joke. But I am not Wu Peifu. Wu Peifu took an oath not to enter the concession. I am engaged in revolution using the methods of a world revolutionary. In the past, I have drifted and wandered to the east, west, north, and south. I can also go abroad immediately in the future, and I can also go to Hong Kong suddenly. Since I fled overseas in the 18th year, I have always been running around in all directions. As long as it is for the revolution, where can I not go? In the time of the Qing Dynasty, we organized the headquarters of the Tongmenghui in Japan. We were not afraid of people saying that we were taking refuge in imperialism and not engaging in revolution. I am even more not afraid of people using the set of internal troubles and foreign enemies to intimidate me. In the time of the Qing Dynasty, we also did not stop the revolution because people said that the revolution would be enough to cause partition. Since I became a revolutionary, I have always been fearless of intimidation. Therefore, holding a meeting in Shanghai and not going to Nanjing is not a problem and has no value for research. In Shanghai, there is still room for the expression of free will. How can we save the country and remove internal troubles and foreign enemies if we go to Nanjing? This level should be replied to Mr. Shen. As for saying that the content of the Peace Conference is public, we have always not failed to make it public, except for a small part, which is not convenient to publish due to diplomatic relations. The rest can be seen in the newspapers every day. The diplomatic process is naturally the responsibility of the Nanjing government, because the Nanjing government has already been recognized internationally. The other diplomatic guidelines and principles will be discussed at this conference, and after a decision is made, it will be handed over to the Nanjing government for implementation. When it comes to facing the national crisis together, of course, we are originally intending to do so. How can we come to Shanghai if we do not seek to face the difficulties together? However, to face the national crisis together, we must also find a way. When we were in Guangdong, we had already said to the people of all circles that we only wanted to find a way for us to die. Should we call Guangdong to send troops to resist Japan? Can the troops pass through the areas under the rule of Nanjing? (This paragraph is roughly the same as the replies to the student and worker representatives, so it is omitted.) Therefore, the fundamental way to deal with foreign affairs is to establish a truly democratic government, and only then can we seek permanent peace in China and never have civil war again. If a democratic government cannot be established and democratic politics cannot be realized, then internal troubles and foreign enemies will be even worse in the future than they are now. Therefore, like the government of the Northern warlords in the past, we certainly want to overthrow it. Like the current Nanjing government, we also express our dissatisfaction in the same way. Because we are dissatisfied, we demand reorganization in order to truly implement political tutelage and establish democracy. Then internal troubles and foreign enemies can be permanently eliminated. How can the current situation of the unification of politics, military, and party be able to eliminate internal troubles and foreign enemies? Since the 18th year, there have been two foreign troubles: the incident on the Middle East Railway, which was confused, casually started a war, and then casually made peace; the second foreign trouble is the current incident in the three northeastern provinces. May I ask, under the current government, the people do not even have the freedom to say a few words about diplomacy. What other way is there to deal with foreign affairs? Therefore, if a government of democracy is not established, internal troubles and foreign enemies cannot be eliminated. Just taking the words of internal troubles and foreign enemies cannot intimidate me. I must use blood to seek the realization of democratic politics and use blood to seek the birth of a democratic government. I am a revolutionary and have long forgotten the existence of life. But perhaps I will say radical things today and go to Nanjing tomorrow, or I will even work together with Mr. Chiang Kai-shek. But I only seek the realization of a democratic government. I am willing to be a small clerk in this government, and I am willing to do so. Freedom of will is endowed by heaven. If there is no opportunity to exercise freedom of will, then it is uncertain whether I will go abroad tomorrow. Regarding my humble opinion, please enlighten me, gentlemen of the intellectual world. If you have anything else to teach me, I am very welcome. (End)

As the enemy's arrogance intensifies, we rely only on slogans and banners to resist. When violence arrives, we order our soldiers to surrender and disarm as if that is the way to resist the enemy. The national situation is critical, and survival is uncertain. Japanese Differentiation of Our Northeast Names 145

▲ Nationals Should Correct This

The Executive Committee of this city issued a circular yesterday, stating: "To whom it may concern: The terms 'Manchuria,' 'Man-Mongolia,' 'South Manchuria,' and 'North Manchuria' are designations used by the Japanese to influence our Eastern Provinces, intending to divide our Northeast from the central provinces, undermine the spirit of unity among the five ethnic groups, and achieve their continental northward expansion policy. Nationals, without being aware, have followed suit, referring to the Three Eastern Provinces as 'Man-Mongolia' or 'Manchuria,' which is highly inappropriate. Hereafter, the Three Eastern Provinces should be uniformly referred to by the names Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, to clarify the situation, avoid falling into their trap, and we hope that you will follow this procedure."

Party and Government Organs Jointly Issue Notice: Labor and Management Should Quickly Seek Coordination 147

▲ Labor and management are not allowed to propose new conditions.

▲ Labor is not allowed to strike or engage in sabotage.

▲ Management is not allowed to dismiss workers without authorization.

Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, and Tao Baichuan, Standing Committee Members of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee, and Zhang, Mayor of the Shanghai Municipal Government, jointly issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Regarding the issuance of this notice, this government has received a telegram from the Ministry of Industry stating that in this time of national crisis, all our countrymen should work together with one heart and await the government's measures. Workers in all areas should strive to produce and overcome difficulties together. All labor disputes should be quickly coordinated, and strikes and sabotage should be strictly prevented. It is hoped that subordinate officials will follow this order and instruct all labor and management organizations to comply. With this approval, this committee and government have jointly agreed on the following three temporary measures to cease disputes between labor and management during this period: (1) All agreements already signed between labor and management should continue to be maintained, and both parties are not allowed to propose new conditions. (2) Except for closures or reductions in the scope of labor due to unavoidable circumstances, management should report to the competent authorities for approval before dismissing workers without authorization. (3) Labor is not allowed to strike or engage in sabotage. If labor or management violate the above, the responsible personnel will be severely punished without leniency. In addition to this committee ordering the Social Affairs Bureau to instruct all labor and management organizations to comply, this joint notice is hereby issued to inform the public and to urge everyone to understand the difficulties of the time, earnestly comply, and not violate this order, so as to avoid any inconvenience. This notice is urgent."

Key News from the Shipping Industry 148

▲ The Xin Jiangtian Experiences Japanese Goods Turmoil: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Jiangtian, on its recent trip from Shanghai to Ningbo, was found to have its teahouse staff and others privately transporting over two hundred and twenty pieces of Japanese salted fish, worth over six thousand yuan. Upon arriving in Ningbo, the goods were unloaded at the dock, at which point a Japanese goods inspection committee privately allowed them to pass. Cold water vendors and workers at the dock were greatly dissatisfied, gathering a crowd of five to six hundred people who tied up the inspectors Xu Zhen and Li He, and twenty others, intending to parade them through the streets. Patrol Captain Wu Zhenhua and others arrived to mediate, releasing the two inspectors Xu and Li. Xu and others fled into the China Merchants Bureau, where bureau staff hid the two and locked the iron gate, which aroused public outrage and the intention to destroy the gate. The turmoil escalated, and the security team dispatched two squads of soldiers to persuade them to desist, promising to hand over the two inspectors to the Public Security Bureau, and to submit the two hundred and twenty pieces of Japanese salted fish to the China Merchants Bureau's 228 warehouse for storage, pending public judgment. Only then did the matter come to a conclusion. Xu and Li, the two inspectors, were injured from being dragged and beaten by the crowd.

▲ No News of the Xin Ning Arriving: The Xin Ninghai, which travels between Ningbo and Ninghai, was attacked on the 3rd of this month at 6:00 AM, sailing through the waters of Xiashan Xue'ao. Over twenty pirates, disguised as farmers and carrying bamboo baskets containing handguns and other weapons, boarded the ship. This was discovered by Lin Yaofu, the ship's security team leader, who tried to prevent them from boarding. The bandits fired three shots, hitting his legs and chest, causing him to fall into a small boat and escape to Haining for medical treatment, but he died. The Xin Ninghai was commandeered by the bandits and sailed north, with over twenty passengers, thirty sailors, and many other crew members all kidnapped. Three days have passed and there is still no news. Although the Outer Sea Hall has dispatched warships to pursue, there is still no news to this day.

British Goods, Yarn, and Raw Materials: The Visitors' Bureau Can Provide Guidance for Ordering 149

▲ Superior to Japanese Goods, Definitely Not Unsuitable

Nationals, in light of Japan's atrocities, are voluntarily severing economic ties with Japan and refusing to import Japanese raw materials. The silk dyeing industry in this city and others are experiencing a raw material panic. The trade association has petitioned the competent authorities for permission to appropriately reduce the number of workers. The Ministry of Industry, believing that this would harm workers' livelihoods and industrial production, did not approve. Yarn and raw materials can also be replaced with British goods. The Ministry of Industry instructed the trade association to comply promptly and stated that the request to dismiss workers or close factories should not be considered. However, the silk dyeing and weaving industry believes there are practical difficulties and requested remedies. According to news from the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Visitors' Bureau, after receiving the order from the Ministry of Industry, the bureau immediately convened various industrial circles to discuss solutions. Regarding yarn and raw materials, although there is currently a large quantity of coarse yarn, the 42-count thread that is usually used can be replaced with 20-count yarn. Furthermore, there is a large stock of two-ply thread produced in Manchester, England, which can also be used as a substitute. If you are unfamiliar with the ordering procedures, the bureau can provide guidance. Moreover, the British raw materials are better than the Japanese goods and will definitely not be unsuitable. If smaller factories do not have the ability to place orders, they may consider placing joint orders, or have the trade association place orders on their behalf. The goods can be shipped to Shanghai approximately one month after ordering. There are already quite a few people who have placed orders.

Disaster Relief Continues Unabated 150

▲ Report from the National Government Flood Disaster Financial Group

A summary report of the income and expenditure situation of the Finance Group of the National Government Relief Flood Disaster Committee up to October 31st:

(A) Income from Relief Donations: This group began soliciting relief donations in mid-August. Thereafter, the income from relief donations was published in Chinese and Western newspapers every ten days, for public notification. As of October 31st, a total of 5,642,103.53 yuan in various currencies was received, including (1) private donations of 168,616.70 yuan (accounting for 3% of the total), (2) group donations of 3,286,011.80 yuan (accounting for 59% of the total), (3) overseas Chinese donations of 1,047,835.71 yuan (accounting for 18% of the total), and (4) foreign donations of 1,139,639.32 yuan (accounting for 20% of the total).

(B) Expenditure of Relief Donations: As of October 31st, the accounting and auditing group of this committee had paid out a total of 5,274,000 yuan, including (1) 3,451,000 yuan distributed to various provinces for emergency relief, including Hubei (1,315,000 yuan), Jiangsu (466,000 yuan), Anhui (340,000 yuan), Jiangxi (333,000 yuan), Henan (313,000 yuan), Hunan (264,000 yuan), Shandong (200,000 yuan), Fujian (50,000 yuan), Guizhou (50,000 yuan), Yunnan (40,000 yuan), Sichuan (40,000 yuan), and Shaanxi (40,000 yuan), (2) 730,000 yuan for clothing, (3) 450,000 yuan for food, (4) 250,000 yuan for medicine, (5) 223,000 yuan for transportation, (6) 150,000 yuan for labor and materials, and (7) 20,000 yuan for miscellaneous expenses.

▲ Regular Meeting of the Provincial Flood Disaster Emergency Relief Association 151

The Shanghai Provincial Flood Disaster Emergency Relief Association held its fifteenth regular meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday. Those in attendance were Xu Shiying, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Ye Kaixin, Li Zizhong, Mao Youfeng, Huang Bodu, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin (represented by Li Zhi'an), Zhang Zhijiang (represented by Weng Guoxun), Wang Yiting, Ha Shaofu, Wu Yunzhai, Li Zuyu, Qi Zhongdao, Gong Jin (representative from Qinghai), Xu Zhixuan, Huang Dingxun, and others. Xu Shiying chaired the meeting and Yang Yunzhen took the minutes. The matters discussed were: (1) Regarding the proposal to publicly appoint general directors of winter emergency relief in various regions in accordance with the association's relief regulations, it was resolved that Feng Yangshan would be appointed for Henan, Zhao Youqin for Hunan, Zhou Baipeng for Jiangxi, Wang Yiting for Zhejiang, Zhang Shaotang for Shandong, Cui Xianlou for Gansu and Shaanxi, Xu Pingxuan for central Anhui, and Zhai Zhancheng for southern Anhui. (2) Regarding the proposal that the association should add one standing committee member to each of the provinces of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Henan, where the disaster situation is particularly severe, to handle affairs in order to ensure progress, it was resolved that Ye Kaixin would be appointed for Hunan, Guan Jiongzhi for Hubei, Hu Youyu for Jiangxi, and Li Zhizhong for Henan, and that this would be submitted to the general assembly for ratification. (3) Zhang Shaotang, Shandong's relief commissioner, stated that the current distribution would require approximately 13,000 yuan, with a remaining 27,000 yuan. It seemed appropriate to select areas with severe disasters and appropriately increase subsidies for seeds and farming tools, or to use all 27,000 yuan to establish two or three porridge kitchens near Jinan, so that disaster victims who had fled elsewhere could avoid freezing and starvation. It was resolved that the porridge kitchens had already been organized by the Red Swastika Society, and the association could appropriately provide seeds and farming tools, but not subsidies. (4) The Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee forwarded a letter from Xu Pingxuan, the association's central Anhui relief commissioner, outlining a winter relief plan budget for 15 counties, including Huaining. The plan estimated that there were over 3.9 million disaster victims, and distributing 20% of the relief funds would require over 780,000 yuan, while providing clothing would require over 390,000 sets of cotton clothes. How should this be reviewed and responded to? It was resolved to hand it over to the general director of central Anhui for review and handling. (5) The Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee forwarded a letter from Xu Pingxuan, the association's central Anhui relief commissioner and representative, stating that winter relief should select areas with severe disasters and appropriately establish nine porridge kitchens for review and handling. It was resolved to handle it in conjunction with the above item. (6) Zhu Ziqiao received a telegram from the Shaanxi Provincial Relief Affairs Association stating that the weather was cold and flood victims were living outdoors, which was very tragic. The association was planning to establish shelters to provide relief and requested a quick allocation of relief funds for implementation. It was resolved to allocate 3% of the relief funds. (7) Wang Tingrui, director of the Qinghai Office in Beijing, telegraphed that the province's relief funds should be handed over to Qi Zhongdao to carry to Qinghai for distribution. It was resolved that the association and Qi Jun should first telegraph the Qinghai Provincial Government to inquire about the handling. (8) According to reports, the Shanghai shelter for disaster victims was planning to be disbanded by the municipal government, which was very pitiful. Should efforts be made to rescue it? (9) The Shanghai Municipal Office for the Reception of Disaster Victims requested an additional allocation of 40,000 to 50,000 yuan to subsidize its maintenance. It was resolved to handle it in conjunction with the previous item and to appoint Ye Kaixin, Qu Wenliu, and Zhu Ziqiao as three representatives to attend a joint meeting of five charitable organizations to jointly plan and handle it. (10) Regarding the date of the executive committee meeting for this month, it was resolved to hold it next Saturday, November 14th, at the association. (11) Qu Wenliu proposed contacting the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association and requested the appointment of representatives. It was resolved to appoint Zhang Xiaolin, Li Zuyu, and Pan Xulun as three representatives to go and contact them. Furthermore, the association had previously contacted Xu Pingxuan, the relief commissioner of central Anhui, via telegram to discuss winter relief matters, and Mr. Xu had arrived in Shanghai yesterday and reported on the progress of the central Anhui relief efforts and the detailed plans for winter relief.

Five Groups Plan to Take Over the Reception of Disaster Victims 152

The Shanghai Municipal Office for the Reception of Disaster Victims, due to the fact that the flood disaster in Jiangbei has not receded and various places have stopped receiving disaster victims, resulting in disaster victims flocking to Shanghai, and for the sake of international image and public security and hygiene, is planning to repatriate disaster victims to their hometowns. Five charitable organizations, including the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the Shanghai Provincial Flood Disaster Emergency Relief Association, the Red Cross Society, the Charitable Organizations Joint Association, and the Jiangsu Flood Disaster Relief Association, held separate meetings yesterday. They all agreed that winter was approaching and that disaster victims returning to their hometowns would be facing concerns about clothing and food. To save lives and solve the problem thoroughly, the five groups planned to take over the reception. At the same time, they still requested assistance from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Health Bureau to facilitate the process. They also planned for each group to appoint three people to convene a joint meeting on the 11th of the month (next Wednesday) to discuss how to proceed.

What Did Bandits Want with a Rented Car? 153

▲ Chauffeur Tied Up in an Attic Room

▲ Job Completed in 45 Minutes

▲ Purpose of Car Rental Unclear

Yesterday morning, at the Xiafei Motor Company on Route Lafayette in the French Concession, a bandit disguised as a customer came to rent a car. As a result, the chauffeur was tied up in a bandit den. By the afternoon, the car was found near the French Garden. However, the true purpose remains unknown. The details are as follows:

▲ Hired to Pick Up a Patient: Yan Hongru, a 42-year-old man from Yangzhou, who invested in the Xiafei Motor Company at 744-746 Route Lafayette in the French Concession, was managing a passable business. At 9:55 AM yesterday morning, an uninvited customer wearing a dark gray gabardine jacket, a light gray felt hat, and speaking in a Cantonese accent came and claimed his name was Wu Zhenhua. He said he needed to rent a car to pick up a patient at 321 Route Doumer and take them to a hospital on North Szechuan Road.

▲ Ordered to Stop Midway: After agreeing to a rental price of $1.50, to be paid after the job was completed, the company's bookkeeper ordered Li Shiqi, a chauffeur from Yangzhou with driver's license number 9104, to drive out in a new Chrysler bridge-style car with license plate number 12495, purchased from the Global Motor Company less than two weeks ago. The uninvited guest sat in the car and headed west. The car drove past Avenue Albert and approached the entrance of the Yiyu Alley near Rue Massenet, when the uninvited guest suddenly ordered the car to stop.

▲ Chauffeur Deceived: After the car stopped at the entrance of Yiyu Alley, the uninvited guest jumped out of the car and asked the chauffeur to accompany him inside to help carry the patient down. The chauffeur also got out of the car and entered the main alley, turned into the first narrow alley, and went straight to the attic room on the third floor through the second back door. As soon as the chauffeur entered the room, he noticed that there was only a bed in the west corner, covered with an old quilt, and nothing else. There were four strong men already inside. As soon as they saw the chauffeur, one of them suddenly pulled out a gun and forbade him from making any noise. The uninvited customer then exited and went downstairs. The chauffeur heard the engine start, as the car had been temporarily "borrowed."

▲ Bandits Fled in Disorder: The men tied the chauffeur's hands behind his back with rope, tightly gagged his mouth with a handkerchief, pushed him onto the bed, and wrapped him in a red blanket. The men then went downstairs together, leaving one person to guard him. After about 45 minutes, the men returned. One of them locked the door from the outside and told the chauffeur not to make any noise, saying that the car would be parked near the French Garden soon and he could find it by address. They then fled in disorder. No one was seen in the direction the car left. After struggling for a long time, the chauffeur managed to untie himself.

▲ Escaped Through Window and Down a Ladder: After the chauffeur untied himself, he looked out the window and called for help. A plasterer happened to have a tall ladder set up near the back door to decorate the walls. The chauffeur, in desperation, climbed out the window and down the ladder, then went around to the front door and learned that it was the Gongxinxie Kee Fresh Fruit Store at 1239 Route Lafayette. He told the store owner about his dangerous experience, but the owner was completely unaware. The chauffeur rushed to report to the Lou-za Police Station, but because the incident took place on Rue Chapsal, he hired a rickshaw to go to Rue Chapsal to report.

▲ The Rental of the House: After hearing the news, the captain immediately ordered Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. According to the fruit store owner, Zhou Boting from Ningbo, the store had just opened the day before yesterday. On the evening of the 4th of this month, two men speaking in a Cantonese accent came and said they were studying at a certain school. They rented the attic room, stating that the monthly rent would be nine yuan and paying a deposit of two yuan. Last night (the previous night), they moved in a bed and said that the rental would start on the 6th and that their older brother would act as a guarantor when the time came. Late that night, three or four more men came. As for everything that happened to the chauffeur upstairs this morning, he had no knowledge because he was on the third floor and the distance was too far.

▲ The Original Car Was Indeed Found: After the chauffeur, accompanied by the detectives, went to investigate, he immediately returned to the company to describe the situation. The company immediately sent several people to search for the car in the French Garden area. By the time they reached the area near Avenue Haig, they indeed saw the car parked by the side of the road. They then reported to the police station. The captain ordered them to drive the car back first and wait for further investigation. However, as of tonight, no kidnapping cases have occurred in the Chinese or French concessions.

New House Collapse in Caojiadu: Fatalities and Injuries 154

▲ Three Men and Women Crushed to Death

▲ Two Injured

At around 4:30 PM the day before yesterday, a newly built building in the Lushuezhai area of Caojiadu in western Shanghai suddenly collapsed completely, resulting in the tragic deaths of three men and women and injuries to two others. The details are as follows:

▲ New Building: Chen Genlin, who lived in Dujiazha, Caojiadu, western Shanghai, had a piece of ancestral land in the Lushuezhai area. The Longjinjie Construction Company contracted to build a three-story building in the previous month. Since construction began, it had been over a month. All the work had to be carried out in accordance with the plans approved by the Works Bureau. The project was 80% complete, with the roof recently finished and the finishing work in progress.

▲ Sudden Collapse: The owner of the construction company, Mr. Long, eager to receive payment, had the roof built before the wall construction was completed, resulting in a top-heavy structure. At 4:00 PM on the day before yesterday, while the workers were working, the building collapsed with a loud crash, shaking the surroundings. The villagers in the area were shocked and fled in panic. The neighboring thatched sheds were also crushed, and five residents were buried under the bricks and tiles, all of whom managed to escape. For a time, dust filled the air, blurring vision.

▲ A Glimpse of the Tragedy: Next to the building was a thatched shed rented by a Mr. Zhang from Jiangbei. The lease had expired last year, and the landlord had repeatedly urged him to move, but Mr. Zhang had repeatedly delayed. It was only now that the tragedy occurred. After the incident, villagers came forward to rescue, removing the bricks and tiles. They found an elderly woman, Ms. Chen (the wife of Mr. Zhang Changyou, 64 years old), and a woman, Ms. Zhang (the daughter of the elderly woman, 46 years old). Both were covered in blood and their brains had been shattered, a truly tragic sight. They had already died. There were also one man and two women injured. The man, Cao Yifu, 24 years old, was a worker hired by the factory. His injuries were severe and he was immediately taken to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. He died early yesterday morning due to his injuries. The two women, one surnamed Wang and one surnamed Tang, were both around 20 years old and from Jiangbei. They were also taken to the hospital for treatment, and it is said that their lives are not in danger.

▲ Aftermath: After the tragedy occurred, the head of the Sixth District Police Station, Director Ren, was notified and immediately sent police officers to rescue and investigate the cause of the collapse. He arrested Wu Xinquan, the accountant of the construction company, Long Fangshi, the wife of the factory owner, and Han Yongru, the guarantor, for further investigation. However, the factory owner, Mr. Long, had already fled without a trace. Later, it was learned that the son of the deceased, Mr. Zhang Shuxiang, had met with misfortune and was responsible for the delay in moving. The factory owner had also fled without a trace. He volunteered to prepare coffins for burial, so the bodies were collected yesterday afternoon. It is rumored that the cause of the collapse was that the factory owner had saved on materials and reduced labor, and had not followed the approved plans.

Zhenru Train Crash: Stationmaster Dismissed and Investigated 155

▲ Switchman Temporarily Detained

According to Mr. Guo Chengen, Director of the Railways Bureau, the Zhenru train crash was investigated by officials sent by the Ministry of Railways a few days ago. The switchman and the stationmaster who were responsible have been dismissed and the switchman has been detained. The Railways Bureau is very sorry for the injured passengers and has sent staff to the hospital to express condolences several times. Regarding the railway staff's pension, half of it has already been issued and the rest will be issued soon.

Second Lottery Held for Downtown Land 157

▲Registration Ended at the End of Last Month, Lottery Held on the 10th for Allotment

▲City Land Bureau Currently Preparing for Third Call for Applications

The first call for applications for land in the city's downtown area was enthusiastically completed last month. The areas originally designated for city government employees and others were not successfully allotted. Therefore, the city government re-designated the downtown area for a second round of applications, which ended at the end of last month. A lottery for allotment will be held on the morning of the 10th of this month. According to statistics from the bureau yesterday, the second designated allotment area comprises 459 mu. After deducting 16 mu claimed by the original owners with priority rights, 443 mu remain. In this round, 101 mu have been registered for by various parties, leaving 342 mu. The Land Bureau has obtained approval from the city government to hold a third call for applications. The registration date is set from the 11th of this month (the day after the second registrants' lottery) to the 25th of this month, with the lottery for allotment set for the 1st of next month. According to the bureau's statement to the New Voice News Agency reporter, the third call for applications is expected to be more enthusiastic than the second. This is because the second call stipulated that each person could only purchase one mu of land, while the third call allows each person to purchase two mu or one mu. Generally, purchasers prefer to buy large tracts of land rather than small plots, so it is expected to be more popular than the second. Furthermore, the city government had designated 209 mu of land in the city center for government employees. After deducting 18 mu reclaimed by the original owners with priority rights, city government employees claimed 96 mu in the second call for applications, leaving over 90 mu. The disposition method for this land has not yet been determined.

Arresting a Bandit with a Cigarette 160

▲Extortionist waved his hand into his pocket

▲Seemingly indicating possession of a handgun

▲Forced to use his right hand to accept the cigarette

▲Detectives then swarmed in and apprehended him

Zhu Jinsheng, a local resident and owner of the Zhu Xingji clothing store at 454 Route Ferguson in western Shanghai, suddenly received a threatening letter from bandits on the afternoon of the 2nd of this month. Upon opening it, a bullet was enclosed. The letter contained threatening language, intending to extort 3,000 yuan. It also stipulated that a room be booked at the Dongya Hotel on Nanjing Road on the afternoon of the 5th, with the name "Zhu Lansheng" on the sign, and someone would come to negotiate. Zhu reported the letter to the Xinzha detention center. The police chief ordered detectives Ruan Yao, Bao Chen Yaoting, and Yang Xinzheng to disguise themselves and accompany Zhu Jinsheng and his accountant Zhao Bing to the Dongya Hotel on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. They booked room 404, with the name "Zhu Lansheng" written outside. Zhu was instructed to stay inside alone, while the others lay in ambush nearby. At 4:30 PM, the bandit gang first called to inquire. Zhao Bing answered, stating that he was a small businessman with limited funds and urging them to come quickly to negotiate. The bandits agreed to arrive within twenty minutes. At around 5:00 PM, a bandit named Fang Shulin from Shanghai entered the room, with his left hand inserted into his pocket, indicating that he seemingly possessed a handgun. He asked Zhu if he had brought the money. Zhu, fearing his weapon, did not dare to act rashly and offered him a cigarette. Fang had no choice but to extend his right hand to accept it. At that moment, the detectives swarmed into the room and apprehended Fang. Fang confessed that a certain Zhou was his accomplice and was waiting in front of the Yile Tian Teahouse. The detectives took Fang Shulin with them, but Zhou had already fled. However, Zhao Gengsheng was apprehended at the entrance of the Wing On Company and taken into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang presented the case and requested a postponement. Zhu Jinsheng and witness Zhao Bing also testified to prove everything. Fang Shulin confessed that he delivered the threatening letter, but Zhou wrote it. Yesterday, Zhou instructed him to go to the Dongya Hotel to collect the money. Zhao Gengsheng confessed that he knew Zhou and met him in Yanziwo yesterday afternoon. Zhou instructed him to go to Nanjing Road to find Fang Shulin. He was arrested in front of the Wing On Company while Zhou escaped. Judge Wu Yanqi verified the confessions and ordered the two defendants to be detained pending a retrial in seven days.

Anti-Drug Association Receives Numerous Reports of Severe Opium Poppy Cultivation in Fujian 166

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has received dozens of letters and telegrams from various sources in southern Fujian, reporting on the cultivation of opium poppies in various counties of Quanzhou, Zhangzhou, Xinghua, and Yongchun. It is said that the key figures behind this are all influential individuals. Zhangzhou can collect 3 million yuan in taxes, Quanzhou can collect 5 million yuan, and Xinghua has already planted 50,000 mu. The distribution of profits has also been agreed upon. Lin Yushi, a member of the Fujian Opium Prohibition Committee, has always been enthusiastic about opium prohibition and is strongly opposed to this large-scale planting of opium seedlings. He has joined all the members of the Opium Prohibition Committee in resigning from the provincial government to demonstrate their determination. According to a report from Quanzhou, an airfield is currently being constructed in Quanzhou to facilitate the export of opium by air. In the future, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Quanzhou, and Zhangzhou can utilize airplanes to export opium, which can be considered a new method of opium trafficking. Opium paste sales have already been implemented in Quanzhou and Zhangzhou, and Xiamen will also be holding them soon. It is reported that the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association and various groups in Fujian will have a serious response to this matter.

Xu Chihen, Zhu Yingpeng, Yu Kongwo, Jiang Jianhou, Fan Jingwu, Tang Demin, Ge Gongzhen, Sun Daosheng, Ma Chonggan, Hu Zhongchi, and Hang Shijun attended. Tang Demin was elected chairman.
